They really only need to be charged once every few days. All rechargeable batteries have a limited life cycle of approximately 300 charges, after which the battery starts to deteriorate rather quickly. By only charging the toothbrush when it actually needs it, you will greatly extend the life of the product.

  300. I've used the [[ASIN:B007ZN5ATQ Philips Sonicare HX5610/30 Essence 5600 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush, Frustration Free Packaging]] for years, and I love it. I don't know why I never thought to get one for my kids, but they've used any number of rotating head and/or battery powered toothbrushes, from [[ASIN:B003CR89FG Arm & Hammer Arm & Hammer Spinbrush Kids My Way Toothbrush, 1 each]] to [[ASIN:B002DGCRNC Colgate Kids Sponge Bob Powered Toothbrush, Extra Soft Bristles, Colors and Styles May Vary]] to [[ASIN:B00BOB89KW Tooth Tunes Jr Kidz Bop Good Feeling Singing Tooth Brush]]. While all of these toothbrushes were adequate, not a single one of them was able to do what this Sonicare has been able to--get my daughter to adequately brush her teeth for a full two minutes. In fact, more often than not, we've had to send her back to the bathroom two, three, or four times to get one full brushing in.<br /><br />This Sonicare Electric Toothbrush for kids is awesome on several levels. For one, it has a built-in timer that plays a very brief tune during the brushing time to let kids know when to switch from one section of the mouth to another (the timing is divided into four equal segments). While you can start a child right off with the timer at two minutes, you can also set it to go into training mode. In this mode, the first brushing is timed at one full minute (4 15-second intervals), with successive brushings adding time until it gets to a full two-minute session each time. As my daughter used to brush her teeth for 15 seconds total and then cry when we told her she needed to re-brush, this has been something of a godsend for us. We don't have to argue with her about how long she did or didn't brush her teeth because the toothbrush does it for us. My own Sonicare has a similar timing feature, but the difference is that on the kids brush the alert to switch quadrants in the mouth is a little bit louder and a little bit longer, so it's hard to miss.<br /><br />What I actually like better on this toothbrush than what I have on mine is the way the brush head attaches. On my older Sonicare, the brushhead inserts into the open end of the handle. It can get pretty nasty in there when water gets down into the handle, and some head changes have had me gagging and questioning whether I want to keep using it. With this toothbrush, the head has the opening while the handle has the part that sticks out. This means water can't accumulate inside the handle because it would run down the outside instead of pooling on the inside.<br /><br />My daughter also loved that she was able to choose her own design for the toothbrush. The sticker pack came with 8 different choices for the main part of the handle, with a bunch of smaller stickers that can be used elsewhere. We haven't made use of the smaller stickers (she wants to find the perfect place for them), but she loves that her toothbrush has a \\"tooth fairy\\" on it. I just love that she is loving brushing her teeth--twice a day, no less!

How did it stack up compared to other Philips models? Did we have any problems? Did we like the stickers? Read on to find out:<br /><br />SET UP AND APPEARANCE: I personally think this is one pretty toothbrush. The accompanying stickers are actually neat; surprising since you don't usually think of Toothbrush makers as the trendiest bunch in the world. You have to charge the brush after you unpack before use; this will take several hours (they recommend overnight). It was in the Set Up stage that we ran into our first problem: There's a weird white plastic panel meant to fit onto the front of the brush. You're supposed to apply whatever sticker you like and then pop the panel into place. For the life of me, I could not get that panel to fasten onto the brush. It just doesn't fit. The panel does not seem to serve any purpose at all, other than a place to apply stickers. Strange. On another topic, I feel for the price point this brush should come with an extra brush head, especially since it's a kid's product and things do happen, like brush heads disappearing down a drain or what have you.<br /><br />PERFORMANCE: The brush, like many Sonicare products, starts off with a \\"low\\" brush speed that increases with each use until a person is accustomed to the brush action. In my opinion, the brush is too forceful even at the beginning stages (I also feel this way about the last two Sonicare products I've tested; the one I'm using now rattles my head). My little charge tried it once, freaked out, then refused to use it again. It is only with much coaxing that I can get her to turn it on for a minute or so, then she shuts it off and uses it like a regular toothbrush (she loves the way it looks, however).<br /><br />CONTROLS: Though there are only three, the control buttons are not intuitive and you will have to read the manual carefully to figure out how to use the features. There is a nice built-in timer that chimes when a two-minute brush cycle is over.<br /><br />RESULTS: I am very convinced of the superiority of electric toothbrushes in general, and in terms of cleaning power I think Sonicare an outstanding brand. Plaque levels especially are much easier to control. I feel it is absolutely worth it to get an electric toothbrush for your kids, as it will probably save you (and them) much grief down the road.<br /><br />In conclusion, a great idea, if you can get your kids to use it. I don't think the brush force is a hazard in anyway, I just think, especially for younger kids, the vibrating brush might be intimidating. The speed really should start out slower and gentler. I think for the price point extra brush heads should be included. I think someone needs to rethink that plastic front panel. I think all my thinking will cost Philips one star and earn them:<br /><br />RATING: Bnual carefully to figure out how to use the features. I have two children, and they've been using the previous model of this toothbrush, [[ASIN:B002CVTVUA Philips Sonicare HX6311/02 Sonicare for Kids Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]], for almost two years. We originally started with Sonicare for Kids at our dentist's recommendation, and since we made the switch, have had nothing but positive comments from our dental hygenists about how well the kids are brushing. Sonicare makes it easy.<br /><br />Anyway, this new version of Sonicare for Kids is almost identical to the previous model. It's blue instead of red, and comes with eight new faceplates to let your child personalize, but it has the same physical body, uses the same charger and toothbrush heads, and - as far as I can tell - has the same motor inside as the previous model. It gives you the option of two different levels of vibration, and features a two-minute timed brushing cycle with beeps every 30 seconds to remind you to switch the brush to a new quadrant of your mouth. If your child has never used a sonic toothbrush before, I highly recommend starting at the lower level of vibration - it's very tickly till you get used to it - and using the training setting, which starts out with shorter brush cycles and gradually builds up to the full two minutes of brushing over a couple of weeks.<br /><br />Though Sonicare hasn't made too many changes to their wonderful toothbrush, there are a couple of minor differences worth mentioning. First, the beeps that let you know when it's time to change where you're brushing play much, much more softly than on the old model, and that's a change that I love. On the negative side, while the former toothbrush came packaged with two different sized brush heads - one smaller sized for kids age 4-7, and one larger sized for kids age 7-10 - this new model came with only the larger sized head. That's probably okay if you have an older child, but if you have a younger one, I highly recommend trying out the smaller sized \\"Compact\\" head,[[ASIN:B00G5L89JM Philips Sonicare HX6032/94 2 Piece Kids Brush Head, Compact]]. My 11 year old son has been using the larger brush heads for several years, but I greatly prefer the smaller heads for my 7 year old, because they fit in her little mouth so much better.

  551. Got this for my son, to help make sure he brushes his teeth long enough. Previously, he would just try to get finished, as quickly as possible. With this brush, not only does he brush for at least two minutes, he will sometimes go longer.<br /><br />The brush is designed to beep every 30 seconds, which is meant to indicate it is time to switch to the next quadrant of your mouth. The idea is nice. However, who brushes their teeth in quadrants? I think most people would divide their brushing into 16ths. You've got the 4 outside sides, the 4 inside sides, the inside bottom front, inside top front, the 4 chewing surfaces, the outside top front and outside bottom front. If you break up the 2 minutes (120 seconds) into 16 parts, it would be 7.5 seconds per section. I think this would also make it easier for kids to not feel like brushing is taking so long.<br /><br />In any case, it is a good toothbrush, and my son really likes it.
